the hypothesis. But if for example `x_1 ‚ąČ ūĚĒ≠`, it suffices, for each index `i` such that `x_i ‚ąą ūĚĒ≠`, to replace `x_i` by
`x_1 + x_i`, in order to have a system of parameters of which no element belongs to `ūĚĒ≠`. Hypothesis a) and the relation
`dim(A/ūĚĒģ) = n` imply, by virtue of `(18.11.5.1)`, that `m ‚Č• n`; one can therefore consider a family
`(x_i)_{1 ‚Č§ i ‚Č§ m}` of elements `x_i ‚ąČ ūĚĒ≠`, of which the first `n` form a system of parameters of `A`. Multiplying
moreover the `x_i` by invertible elements `u_i` of `A`, one can, thanks to `(18.11.5.2)`, suppose that the images of
the `dx_i` (`1 ‚Č§ i ‚Č§ m`) in `(ő©_{A/k}^1)_ūĚĒ≠` generate this `A_ūĚĒ≠`-module, and the multiplication by the `u_i` has not
altered the fact that the `x_i` for `1 ‚Č§ i ‚Č§ n` form a system of parameters. Let us then consider the local
`k`-homomorphism `u : B ‚Üí A` such that `u(T_i) = x_i` for `1 ‚Č§ i ‚Č§ m` (Bourbaki, Alg. comm., chap. III, ¬ß4, n¬į 5,
prop. 6); since the `x_i` generate an ideal of definition of `A`, it results from `(0_I, 7.4.4 and 7.4.3)` that `u`
makes `A` into a finite `B`-algebra. One therefore has `(18.11.3.5)` the exact sequence

```text
  (ő©_{B/k}^1 ‚äó_B A) ‚Üí^v ő©_{A/k}^1 ‚Üí ő©_{A/B}^1 ‚Üí 0.
```

But the `dx_i` are the canonical images by `v` of the elements `dT_i ‚äó 1` `(0, 20.5.2.6)`. If one localizes the
preceding exact sequence at `ūĚĒ≠`, one sees therefore that `v_ūĚĒ≠ : (ő©_{B/k}^1 ‚äó_B A)_ūĚĒ≠ ‚Üí (ő©_{A/k}^1)_ūĚĒ≠` is surjective, and
consequently one has `(ő©_{A/B}^1)_ūĚĒ≠ = (ő©_{A/B}^1)_ūĚĒĮ = 0` (where `ūĚĒĮ` is the inverse image of `ūĚĒ≠` in `B`,
cf. `(16.4.15)`). By virtue of `(17.4.1)`, this implies property b) of `(18.11.5)`. Q.E.D.

**Remark (18.11.6).** ‚ÄĒ In the statement of `(18.11.5)`, one cannot suppress the hypothesis `ūĚĒ≠ ‚Č† ūĚĒ™`. Indeed, for every
local `k`-homomorphism `u : B ‚Üí A`, where `B = k[[T_1, ‚Ä¶, T_r]]` (`r` an arbitrary integer) making `A` into a finite
`B`-algebra, `ūĚĒ™` is the only point of `Spec(A)` above the maximal ideal `ūĚĒę` of `B`; the morphism
`Spec(A) ‚Üí Spec(B)` cannot be unramified at `ūĚĒ™` unless `A/ūĚĒę A` is a field, separable extension of `k` `(17.4.1)`, which
implies that the residue field `K` of `A` is a separable extension of `k`. If this condition is not satisfied, the
conclusion of `(18.11.5)` can never be verified for `ūĚĒ≠ = ūĚĒ™`, whatever the integer `m`.

**Corollary (18.11.7).**

<!-- label: IV.18.11.7 -->

*Let `k` be a field, `A` a complete Noetherian local equidimensional `k`-algebra, whose residue field is a finite
extension of `k`, `ūĚĒ≠` a prime ideal of `A`. Then the minimum number of generators of the `A_ūĚĒ≠`-module `(ő©_{A/k}^1)_ūĚĒ≠` is
at least equal to `dim(A)`.*

It is a particular case of `(18.11.5.1)`.

More particularly:

<!-- original page 177 -->

**Corollary (18.11.8).**

<!-- label: IV.18.11.8 -->

*Let `k` be a field, `A` a complete Noetherian local integral `k`-algebra, whose residue field is a finite extension of
`k`. If `K` is the field of fractions of `A`, one has `rg_K((ő©_{A/k}^1) ‚äó_A K) ‚Č• dim(A)`.*

It suffices to set `ūĚĒ≠ = 0` in `(18.11.7)`.

**Corollary (18.11.9).**

<!-- label: IV.18.11.9 -->

*Let `k` be a field, `A` a complete Noetherian local `k`-algebra of dimension `n`, whose residue field is a finite
extension of `k`. Let `ūĚĒ≠` be a prime ideal of `A` distinct from the maximal ideal, and containing a minimal prime ideal
`ūĚĒģ` such that `dim(A/ūĚĒģ) = n`. Suppose that the `A_ūĚĒ≠`-module `(ő©_{A/k}^1)_ūĚĒ≠` admits `n` generators. Then:*

*(i) the `A_ūĚĒ≠`-module `(ő©_{A/k}^1)_ūĚĒ≠` is free of rank `n`.*

*(ii) There exists a local `k`-homomorphism `u : B ‚Üí A`, where `B = k[[T_1, ‚Ä¶, T_n]]`, making `A` into a finite
`B`-algebra, and such that the corresponding morphism `Spec(A) ‚Üí Spec(B)` is √©tale at the point `ūĚĒ≠`.*

*(iii) The `k`-algebra `A_ūĚĒ≠` is geometrically regular.*

Let us prove first (ii); by virtue of `(18.11.5)`, there exists a local homomorphism `u : B = k[[T_1, ‚Ä¶, T_n]] ‚Üí A`
making `A` into a finite `B`-algebra, and such that the corresponding morphism `Spec(A) ‚Üí Spec(B)` is unramified at the
point `ūĚĒ≠`; set `ūĚĒĮ = u‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(ūĚĒ≠)`. The hypothesis on `ūĚĒģ ‚äā ūĚĒ≠`, and the fact that `A` is a quotient of a regular ring
`(0, 19.8.8)` imply that one has `dim(A_ūĚĒ≠) = n ‚ąí dim(A/ūĚĒ≠)` `(0, 16.5.12)`. One has similarly
`dim(B_ūĚĒĮ) = n ‚ąí dim(B/ūĚĒĮ)`. Finally, since the morphism `Spec(A) ‚Üí Spec(B)` is unramified at the point `ūĚĒ≠`, the fibre
of this morphism at the point `ūĚĒĮ` is of dimension `0`, hence `(0, 16.3.9)` one has `dim(A/ūĚĒ≠) ‚Č§ dim(B/ūĚĒĮ)` and
consequently `dim(B_ūĚĒĮ) ‚Č§ dim(A_ūĚĒ≠)`. One concludes therefore from `(18.10.1)` that the morphism `Spec(A) ‚Üí Spec(B)` is
√©tale at the point `ūĚĒ≠`.

Assertion (iii) results from the fact that `A_ūĚĒ≠` is formally smooth over `B_ūĚĒĮ` and that `B_ūĚĒĮ` is formally smooth over
`k` (for the preadic topologies) `(0, 19.3.4 and 19.3.5)`, hence `A_ūĚĒ≠` is formally smooth over `k` for its preadic
topology, and consequently is geometrically regular over `k` `(0, 22.5.8)`.

Let us prove finally (i). Let `k'` be an algebraically closed extension of `k`, and consider the semi-local
`k'`-algebra `√ā' = A ‚äóŐā_k k'`. If one considers `A` as a finite `B`-module by means of the homomorphism `u`, one can
write, up to a canonical isomorphism, `√ā' = A ‚äó_B (B ‚äóŐā_k k')` (`(7.5.7.1)`, in the statement of which one recalls that
it is not necessary to suppose the residue field of `B` to be a finite extension of `k`). Set `B' = B ‚äóŐā_k k'`, which
identifies canonically with the formal power series algebra `k'[[T_1, ‚Ä¶, T_n]]`. Since the morphism
`Spec(A) ‚Üí Spec(B)` is finite and √©tale at the point `ūĚĒ≠`, the morphism `Spec(√ā') ‚Üí Spec(B')` is finite, and √©tale at
every point `ūĚĒ≠'` above `ūĚĒ≠` `(17.3.3)`; moreover, `√ā'` is direct composite of local rings `A'_i` of dimension `n`
(`1 ‚Č§ i ‚Č§ r`) `(18.11.4)` and `ūĚĒ≠'` identifies with a prime ideal `ūĚĒ≠'_i` of one of the `A'_i`. The same reasoning as
above proves then that `(A'_i)_{ūĚĒ≠'_i}` is geometrically regular over `k'`, and since `k'` is perfect, it results from
`(18.11.3)` that `(ő©Őā_{A'_i/k'}^1)_{ūĚĒ≠'_i}` is a `(A'_i)_{ūĚĒ≠'_i}`-module free of finite type. But

<!-- original page 178 -->

since `(A'_i)_{ūĚĒ≠'_i}` is isomorphic to `(ő©_{A/k}^1)_ūĚĒ≠ ‚äó_{A_ūĚĒ≠} (A'_i)_{ūĚĒ≠'_i}` `(18.11.4)` and `(A'_i)_{ūĚĒ≠'_i}` is an
`A_ūĚĒ≠`-module faithfully flat, one sees that `(ő©_{A/k}^1)_ūĚĒ≠` is an `A_ūĚĒ≠`-module free of finite type `(2.5.2)`;
moreover, by virtue of `(18.11.5.1)` and of the hypothesis `dim(A/ūĚĒģ) = n`, one concludes that `(ő©_{A/k}^1)_ūĚĒ≠` is an
`A_ūĚĒ≠`-module free of rank `n`. Q.E.D.

**Theorem (18.11.10).**

<!-- label: IV.18.11.10 -->

*Let `k` be a field of characteristic exponent `p`, `A` a complete Noetherian local `k`-algebra, whose residue field is
a finite extension of `k`, `ūĚĒ≠` a prime ideal of `A` distinct from the maximal ideal. The following conditions are
equivalent:*

*a) For every extension `k'` of `k`, and every prime ideal `ūĚĒ≠'` of `√ā' = A ‚äóŐā_k k'` above `ūĚĒ≠`, `√ā'_{ūĚĒ≠'}` is a regular
ring.*

*a') There exist a perfect extension `k'` of `k` and a prime ideal `ūĚĒ≠'` of `√ā' = A ‚äóŐā_k k'` above `ūĚĒ≠`, such that
`√ā'_{ūĚĒ≠'}` is regular.*

*b) Let `n` be the largest of the dimensions of the irreducible components of `Spec(A)` to which `ūĚĒ≠` belongs; then
`(ő©_{A/k}^1)_ūĚĒ≠` is an `A_ūĚĒ≠`-module free of rank `n`.*

*Suppose moreover that `n = dim(A)` (which will be the case if `A` is equidimensional); then the preceding conditions
are also equivalent to:*

*c) There exists a local `k`-homomorphism `u : B ‚Üí A`, where `B = k[[T_1, ‚Ä¶, T_n]]`, making `A` into a finite
`B`-algebra, and such that the corresponding morphism `Spec(A) ‚Üí Spec(B)` is √©tale at the point `ūĚĒ≠`.*

*Each of the conditions a), a'), b) implies the following:*

*d) The ring `A_ūĚĒ≠` is geometrically regular over `k`.*

*If moreover `[k : k^p] < +‚ąě`, condition d) is equivalent to a), a') and b).*

The fact that d) implies b) when `[k : k^p] < +‚ąě` is none other than `(18.11.3)`. It is clear that a) implies trivially
a'); let us show that c) implies a) when `dim(A) = n`. With the notations of a), one has then `√ā' = A ‚äó_B B'`, where
`B' = B ‚äóŐā_k k' = k'[[T_1, ‚Ä¶, T_n]]` `(7.5.7.1)`. The morphism `Spec(√ā') ‚Üí Spec(B')` is then finite and √©tale at the
point `ūĚĒ≠'`, and the reasoning that proves `(18.11.9, (iii))` shows that `√ā'_{ūĚĒ≠'}` is regular.

The fact that b) implies c) when `dim(A) = n` results from `(18.11.9)`. Let us show that a') implies b) when
`dim(A) = n`. One knows that `√ā'` is an `A`-module flat `(18.11.4)` and `dim(√ā') = dim(A) = n`; it results from
`(2.3.4)` and from `(6.1.1)` that there exists a minimal prime ideal `ūĚĒģ'` of `√ā'` contained in `ūĚĒ≠'`, above `ūĚĒģ` and such
that `dim(√ā'/ūĚĒģ') = dim(A/ūĚĒģ) = n`. Moreover, it results from `(18.11.4)` that
`(ő©Őā_{√ā'/k'}^1)_{ūĚĒ≠'} = (ő©_{A/k}^1)_ūĚĒ≠ ‚äó_{A_ūĚĒ≠} √ā'_{ūĚĒ≠'}`; since `k'` is perfect, the hypothesis that `√ā'_{ūĚĒ≠'}` is regular
implies that it is geometrically regular over `k'` `(6.7.7)`. Since `k'^p = k'`, one can apply to `√ā'` and `ūĚĒ≠'` the fact
that d) implies b), hence `(ő©Őā_{√ā'/k'}^1)_{ūĚĒ≠'}` is an `√ā'_{ūĚĒ≠'}`-module free of rank `n`; by faithful flatness
`(18.11.4 and 2.5.2)`, one concludes that `(ő©_{A/k}^1)_ūĚĒ≠` is an `A_ūĚĒ≠`-module free of rank `n`.

This shows the equivalence of a), a'), b) and c) when `dim(A) = n`. It remains to prove that a), a') and b) are still
equivalent in the general case. Let `ūĚĒć` be the ideal of `A`, kernel of the canonical homomorphism `A ‚Üí A_ūĚĒ≠`, and set
`A_1 = A/ūĚĒć`; one has necessarily `ūĚĒć ‚äā ūĚĒ≠`, and if one sets `ūĚĒ≠_1 = ūĚĒ≠/ūĚĒć`, the canonical homomorphism `A_ūĚĒ≠ ‚Üí (A_1)_{ūĚĒ≠_1}`
is bijective; one concludes `(I, 6.5.4)` that the canonical injection `Spec(A_1) ‚Üí Spec(A)` is a local isomorphism at
the point `ūĚĒ≠_1`, and one has `ūĚĒć_ūĚĒ≠ = 0`. One sees as in `(18.11.3)` that one has an exact sequence

```text
  (ūĚĒć/ūĚĒć^2) ‚Üí^j ő©_{A/k}^1 ‚äó_A A_1 ‚Üí ő©_{A_1/k}^1 ‚Üí 0
```

<!-- original page 179 -->

and localizing at `ūĚĒ≠`, there comes an isomorphism `(ő©_{A/k}^1)_ūĚĒ≠ = (ő©_{A_1/k}^1)_{ūĚĒ≠_1}`. This shows that condition b)
for the ring `A` and the ideal `ūĚĒ≠` is equivalent to condition b) for the ring `A_1` and the ideal `ūĚĒ≠_1`. On the other
hand, with the notations of a), one has `√ā'_1 = A_1 ‚äóŐā_k k' = √ā'/ūĚĒć √ā'` up to isomorphism (`(7.5.7.1)`, where the
hypothesis on the residue field of `B` is superfluous); if `ūĚĒ≠'` is a prime ideal of `√ā'` above `ūĚĒ≠`, every element of
`ūĚĒć √ā'` annihilates an element of `√ā' ‚ąí ūĚĒ≠'`, hence `ūĚĒć √ā' ‚äā ūĚĒ≠'`, and if one sets `ūĚĒ≠'_1 = ūĚĒ≠'/ūĚĒć √ā'`, `ūĚĒ≠'_1` is above `ūĚĒ≠_1`
and `(√ā'_1)_{ūĚĒ≠'_1}` identifies canonically with `√ā'_{ūĚĒ≠'}`; this shows therefore that condition a) (resp. a')) for the
ring `A` and the ideal `ūĚĒ≠` is equivalent to condition a) (resp. a')) for the ring `A_1` and the ideal `ūĚĒ≠_1`. Now, all
the minimal prime ideals of `A` contained in `ūĚĒ≠` contain `ūĚĒć` since `Spec(A_1) ‚Üí Spec(A)` is a local isomorphism at the
point `ūĚĒ≠_1`; on the other hand the ideals of `Ass_A(A/ūĚĒć)` are the ideals of `Ass(A)` which are contained in `ūĚĒ≠`
(Bourbaki, Alg. comm., chap. IV, ¬ß1, n¬į 2, prop. 6); so the minimal prime ideals of `A_1` are all contained in `ūĚĒ≠_1`,
and one has consequently `dim(A_1) = n`. It then suffices to apply to `A_1` and to `ūĚĒ≠_1` what has been proved above.

**Remarks (18.11.11).** ‚ÄĒ (i) The equivalence of conditions d) and b) in `(18.11.10)` is no longer valid when one no
longer supposes that `[k : k^p] < +‚ąě`. Indeed, in the example of `(0, 22.7.7, (ii))`, the ring `B = A/ūĚĒģ` is integral and
of dimension `1`; on the other hand, the sequence

```text
  (ūĚĒģ/ūĚĒģ^2) ‚äó_A L ‚Üí^j ő©_{A/k}^1 ‚äó_A L ‚Üí ő©_{B/k}^1 ‚äó_B L ‚Üí 0
```

is exact (same proof as in `(18.11.3)`), and one knows that `j` is not injective, hence `j = 0` since `(ūĚĒģ/ūĚĒģ^2) ‚äó_A L`
is of rank `1`. One concludes that `rg_L(ő©_{B/k}^1 ‚äó_B L) = 2`. Since `B_ūĚĒ≠` is a geometrically regular `k`-algebra, one
sees that here condition d) does not imply b).

(ii) The notations being those of `(18.11.10)`, suppose that `n = dim(A)` and let `(x_i)_{1 ‚Č§ i ‚Č§ n}` be a system of
parameters of `A` not belonging to `ūĚĒ≠`; one deduces from it a local `k`-homomorphism `u : B ‚Üí A` such that
`u(T_i) = x_i` for `1 ‚Č§ i ‚Č§ n`, making `A` into a finite `B`-algebra. In order that the corresponding morphism
`Spec(A) ‚Üí Spec(B)` be √©tale at the point `ūĚĒ≠`, it is necessary and sufficient that the images of the `dx_i` in
`(ő©_{A/k}^1)_ūĚĒ≠` form a system of generators of this `A_ūĚĒ≠`-module. Indeed, one has seen in the proof of `(18.11.5)` that
if the morphism `Spec(A) ‚Üí Spec(B)` is unramified at the point `ūĚĒ≠`, the canonical homomorphism
`(ő©_{B/k}^1 ‚äó_B A)_ūĚĒ≠ ‚Üí (ő©_{A/k}^1)_ūĚĒ≠` is surjective and the images of the elements `dT_i ‚äó 1`, which generate
`ő©_{B/k}^1 ‚äó_B A`, are the `dx_i`, whence the necessity of the condition. Conversely, the same reasoning shows that if
this condition is verified, the morphism `Spec(A) ‚Üí Spec(B)` is unramified at `ūĚĒ≠`, and the reasoning of `(18.11.9)`
proves in fact that this morphism is √©tale at `ūĚĒ≠`.

**Corollary (18.11.12).**

<!-- label: IV.18.11.12 -->

*Let `k` be a field of characteristic exponent `p` such that `[k : k^p] < +‚ąě`, `A` a complete Noetherian local and
integral `k`-algebra, which is not a field, and whose residue field is a finite extension of `k`. There then exists a
finite radicial extension `k'` of `k` such that, setting `√ā' = A ‚äóŐā_k k'`, the `k'`-algebra `√ā'_{red}` and the prime
ideal `0` of this algebra verify the equivalent conditions a), a'), b), c) and d) of `(18.11.10)`. In particular, if
`n = dim(A) = dim(√ā')`,*

<!-- original page 180 -->

*there exists a local `k'`-homomorphism `B' = k'[[T_1, ‚Ä¶, T_n]] ‚Üí √ā'_{red}` making `√ā'_{red}` into a finite `B'`-algebra,
and such that the field of fractions `K'` of `√ā'_{red}` is a finite separable extension of the field of fractions
`k'((T_1, ‚Ä¶, T_n))` of `B'`.*

The morphism `Spec(√ā') ‚Üí Spec(A)` being radicial and finite, `√ā'` is a complete local ring and its nilradical is the
only prime ideal above the ideal `0` of `A`; by flatness, `√ā'` identifies with a subring of `K ‚äó_k k'`, which is
moreover the total ring of fractions of `√ā'`; one has consequently `K' = (K ‚äó_k k')_{red}`. It is a question of
proving, in view of the equivalence d) `‚áĒ` c) of `(18.11.10)`, that there exists a finite radicial extension `k'` of
`k` such that `(K ‚äó_k k')_{red}` is a separable extension of `k'` `(6.7.6)`. Now one knows `(0, 19.8.9)` that under the
hypotheses made, there exists a sub-`k`-algebra `C = k[[T_1, ‚Ä¶, T_n]]` of `A` such that `A` is a finite `C`-algebra; `K`
is therefore a finite extension of the field of fractions `K_1 = k((T_1, ‚Ä¶, T_n))` of `C`, which is separable over `k`
`(0, 21.9.6.4)`. If `p` is the characteristic exponent of `k`, one can therefore write
`K ‚äó_k k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě} = K ‚äó_{K_1} (K_1 ‚äó_k k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě})` and `K_1 ‚äó_k k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě}` is a field, radicial extension of `K_1`; one
concludes that `K ‚äó_k k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě}` is a finite algebra over the field `K_1 ‚äó_k k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě}`, hence an Artinian ring. The
conclusion therefore results from the following more general lemma:

**Lemma (18.11.12.1).** *Let `k` be a field of characteristic `p > 0`, `K` an extension of `k`. The following conditions
are equivalent:*

*a) The ring `K ‚äó_k k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě}` is Artinian.*

*b) There exists an extension `k'` of `k` of finite type such that `(K ‚äó_k k')_{red}` is a separable `k'`-algebra.*

*c) There exists a finite radicial extension `k'` of `k` such that `(K ‚äó_k k')_{red}` is a separable extension of `k'`.*

Let us first show that c) implies a). The ring `A = K ‚äó_k k'` is then a local Artinian ring, and if `ūĚĒĎ` is its
nilradical, the residue field `L = A/ūĚĒĎ` is separable over `k'`; consequently `L ‚äó_k k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě}` is a field, and since it
is equal to `(A ‚äó_k k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě})_{red} = (A/ūĚĒĎ)(‚äó_k k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě})`, one sees that `ūĚĒĎ ‚äó_k k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě}` is the nilradical of
`A ‚äó_k k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě} = K ‚äó_k k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě}`; since `ūĚĒĎ` is an ideal of finite type, the nilradical of `K ‚äó_k k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě}` is therefore
of finite type, which implies that the ring `K ‚äó_k k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě}` is Artinian.

Conversely, let us prove that a) implies c). Let `ūĚĒĎ` be the nilradical of the Artinian local ring `B = K ‚äó_k k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě}`,
which is by hypothesis generated by a finite number of elements of the form `z_i = ‚ąĎ őĽ_{ij} ‚äó őĺ_{ij}`, where
`őĽ_{ij} ‚ąą K`, `őĺ_{ij} ‚ąą k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě}`. Let `k'` be the finite radicial extension of `k` generated by the `őĺ_{ij}`, `ūĚĒĎ_0` the
ideal of `B_0 = K ‚äó_k k'` generated by the `z_i`; it is clear that the `z_i` are nilpotent in `B_0`; on the other hand,
one has `ūĚĒĎ_0 ‚äó_{k'} k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě} = ūĚĒĎ`, and consequently `ūĚĒĎ ‚ą© B_0 = ūĚĒĎ_0`, hence `ūĚĒĎ_0` contains the nilradical of `B_0`, hence
it is equal to it. Since `B/ūĚĒĎ = (B_0/ūĚĒĎ_0) ‚äó_{k'} k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě}` is reduced, one concludes that
`B_0/ūĚĒĎ_0 = (K ‚äó_k k')_{red}` is separable over `k'` `(4.6.1)`.

It is clear that c) implies b). Conversely, suppose b) verified, and note that there exists a separable extension `k_1`
of `k` such that `k'` is a finite radicial extension of `k_1`; set `K_1 = K ‚äó_k k_1`, which is a field. Applying the
equivalence of a) and c) to the extension `K_1` of `k_1`, one sees that `K_1 ‚äó_{k_1} k_1^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě}` is an Artinian ring;
but this ring is equal

<!-- original page 181 -->

to `K ‚äó_k k_1^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě} = (K ‚äó_k k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě}) ‚äó_{k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě}} k_1^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě}`, hence `K ‚äó_k k^{p‚ĀĽ‚ąě}` is also Artinian (Bourbaki,
Alg. comm., chap. I, ¬ß3, n¬į 5, cor. of prop. 8); one has thus proved that b) implies a), which finishes the proof of
`(18.11.12.1)` and of `(18.11.12)`.


### 18.12. Applications of √©tale localization to quasi-finite morphisms (generalizations of earlier results)

The results of this number have been communicated to us by P. Deligne.

**Theorem (18.12.1).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.1 -->

*Let `f : X ‚Üí Y` be a morphism locally of finite type, `x` a point of `X`, `y = f(x)`. Suppose that `x` is an isolated
point of the space `f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y)`. Then, there exist an √©tale morphism `Y' ‚Üí Y`, a point `x'` of `X' = X √ó_Y Y'` above `x`
and an open neighbourhood `V'` of `x'` in `X'` such that, if `f' = f_{(Y')} : X' ‚Üí Y'`, `f' | V'` is a finite morphism.
If moreover `f` is separated, `V'` is both open and closed, and `X'` is therefore the sum of two sub-preschemes induced
on opens of `X'`, of which one is finite over `Y'` and contains `x'`.*

The last assertion results from the fact that, if `f` is separated, the same is true of `f'`; so, if `j' : V' ‚Üí X'` is
the canonical injection, the fact that the morphism `f' | V' = f' ‚ąė j'` is finite implies that the same is true of `j'`
`(II, 6.1.5)`, and consequently `V' = j'(V')` is closed in `X'` `(II, 6.1.10)`.

The question being local on `X`, one can suppose `Y = Spec(A)` and `X = Spec(B)` affine, `B` being an `A`-algebra of
finite type, hence of the form `C/ūĚĒć`, where `C = A[T_1, ‚Ä¶, T_r]` and `ūĚĒć` is an ideal of `C`; `f` is therefore separated,
and one can moreover suppose that `f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y) = {x}`. Let `(ūĚĒć_őĽ)` be the family of ideals of finite type of `C` contained in
`ūĚĒć`, so that `ūĚĒć` is the filtered union of the `ūĚĒć_őĽ`. If `X` and the `X_őĽ = Spec(C/ūĚĒć_őĽ)` are considered as closed
sub-preschemes of `Z = Spec(C)`, one has therefore, for the underlying spaces, `X = ‚čā X_őĽ`; if
`f_őĽ : X_őĽ ‚Üí Y` is the structural morphism, one deduces that `f_őĽ‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y) = ‚čā f_őĽ‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y)`, and since the sets `f_őĽ‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y)` are
closed in the Noetherian space `Z_y = Spec(k(y)[T_1, ‚Ä¶, T_r])`, there exists an index `őĽ` such that
`f_őĽ‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y) = f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y) = {x}`. One can therefore suppose that the `X_őĽ` verify the same condition as `X` at the point `x`;
if one proves the proposition for such an `X_őĽ`, it will result for `X`, since if `x'` is a point above `x` in
`Z' = Z √ó_Y Y'`, `X'_őĽ = p‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(X_őĽ)`, where `p : Z' ‚Üí Z` is the projection (so that one has also `X' = p‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(X)`), if there
exists an open neighbourhood `V'_őĽ` of `x'` in `X'_őĽ` which is finite over `Y'`, a fortiori the restriction of `f'_őĽ` to
the closed sub-prescheme `X' ‚ą© V'_őĽ` of `V'_őĽ` will be a finite morphism. One is therefore reduced to the case where
`f` is of finite presentation. Note moreover that the set of points of `X` isolated in their fibre is open in `X`
`(13.1.4)`, so `f` is quasi-finite at the point `x`, and one can consequently restrict to the case where `f` is
quasi-finite. Let `A^h` be the Henselized local ring of `ūĚí™_{Y,y}`, and set `Y^h = Spec(A^h)`. If `X^h = X √ó_Y Y^h`,
`f^h = f_{(Y^h)} : X^h ‚Üí Y^h` is separated, quasi-finite and of finite presentation; since `A^h` is Henselian, there is
for every `x^h ‚ąą X^h` above `x` an open and closed neighbourhood `V^h` of `x^h` in `X^h` which is finite over `Y^h`
`(18.5.11, c))`; since the immersion `V^h ‚Üí X^h` is open and closed, it is quasi-compact, hence of finite presentation
`(1.6.2)`, so `f^h | V^h` is of finite presentation.

This being so, by definition, `A^h` is the inductive limit of a filtered family `(A_őĪ)` of strictly essentially √©tale
`ūĚí™_{Y,y}`-algebras `(18.6.5)`; each `A_őĪ` is itself the inductive limit of a filtered family `(B_{őĪő≤})` of √©tale
`ūĚí™_{Y,y}`-algebras (`(18.6.1)` and `(8.1.2, a))`). Finally, since `B_{őĪő≤}` may be supposed an `ūĚí™_{Y,y}`-algebra of
finite presentation, it results moreover from `(8.1.2, a))` and from `(17.7.8)` that `B_{őĪő≤}` is the inductive limit of
a filtered family `(C_{őĪő≤ő≥})` of √©tale `A`-algebras. Finally, one sees, using the theorem of the double inductive
limit, that `Y^h` is the projective limit of a filtered family `(Y_őĪ)` of affine schemes √©tale over `Y`. If `x_őĪ` is the
projection of `x^h` onto `X_őĪ = X √ó_Y Y_őĪ`, one can suppose that the neighbourhood `V^h`, which is quasi-compact, is of
the form `V_őĪ √ó_{Y_őĪ} Y^h` where `V_őĪ` is an open neighbourhood of `x_őĪ` in `X_őĪ` `(8.2.11)`. Finally, `V^h` being of
finite presentation over `Y^h`, one concludes from `(8.10.5, (x))` that for a suitable `őĪ`, `V_őĪ` is finite over `Y_őĪ`.
Q.E.D.

**Remark (18.12.2).** ‚ÄĒ In the preceding proof, one sees (taking account of `(18.6.2)`) that one has constructed a `Y'`
answering the question, and such moreover that if `y' = f'(x')`, the homomorphism `k(y) ‚Üí k(y')` is bijective.

**Corollary (18.12.3).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.3 -->

*Let `f : X ‚Üí Y` be a morphism locally of finite type and separated, `y` a point of `Y` such that the subspace
`f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y)` is finite and discrete. There then exist an √©tale morphism `Y' ‚Üí Y`, a point `y' ‚ąą Y'` above `y`, such that
`k(y') = k(y)`, and a decomposition of `X'` into the sum of two sub-preschemes `X'_1`, `X'_2` induced on opens of `X'`,
such that the restriction of `f' = f_{(Y')} : X' ‚Üí Y'` to `X'_1` is a finite morphism and one has
`X'_2 ‚ą© f'‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y') = ‚ąÖ`.*

If `n` is the number of points of `f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y)`, one reasons by recurrence on `n`, the corollary being trivial for `n = 0`.
Let `x` be a point of `f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y)`; by virtue of `(18.12.1)` and `(18.12.2)` there is an √©tale morphism `Y_1 ‚Üí Y`, a point
`y_1` of `Y_1` above `y` such that `k(y_1) = k(y)`, and if one sets `S_1 = X √ó_Y Y_1`, `f_1 = f_{(Y_1)} : S_1 ‚Üí Y_1`,
there exists a point `x_1` of `f_1‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y_1)`

<!-- original page 182 -->

such that `S_1` is the sum of two opens `V_1`, `X_1`, `V_1` being finite over `Y_1` and a neighbourhood of `x_1`. By
virtue of the relation `k(y_1) = k(y)`, the fibre `f_1‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y_1)` in `S_1` is isomorphic to `f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y)`, so
`X_1 ‚ą© f_1‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y_1)` is finite, discrete and has `n ‚ąí 1` points. Since `f_1 | X_1` is locally of finite type and
separated, one applies the hypothesis of recurrence to this morphism: there is an √©tale morphism `Y' ‚Üí Y_1`, a point
`y' ‚ąą Y'` above `y_1` such that `k(y') = k(y_1)`, and, if `X' = X √ó_Y Y'` and if `p : X' ‚Üí S_1` is the canonical
projection, one has a decomposition of `p‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(X_1)` into a sum of two sub-preschemes `U'` and `X'_2` induced on opens of
`X'` such that `X'_2 ‚ą© f'‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y') = ‚ąÖ` and that `U'` is finite over `Y'`. Moreover, `V' = p‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(V_1)` is finite over `Y'`
and `X'` is the sum of `U'`, `V'` and `X'_2`; one will therefore answer the question by taking `X'_1` to be the sum of
`U'` and `V'`.

The following corollary improves `(8.11.1)`:

**Corollary (18.12.4).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.4 -->

*In order that a morphism `f : X ‚Üí Y` be finite, it is necessary and sufficient that it be separated, universally
closed, locally of finite type and that, for every `y ‚ąą Y`, `f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y)` be a finite discrete space; in particular, a proper
and quasi-finite morphism is finite.*

Indeed, one can apply corollary `(18.12.3)` to an arbitrary point `y` of `Y`. With the notations of that corollary, `f'`
is a closed morphism, so, since `X'_2` is closed in `X'`, `f'(X'_2)` is closed in `Y'` and does not contain `y'`; there
consequently exists an open neighbourhood `U'` of `y'` in `Y'` such that `U' ‚Üí Y` is of finite type and that
`f'‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(U') = X √ó_Y U'` is finite over `U'`. Let `U` be the image of `U'` in `Y`, which is an open of `Y` by virtue of
`(11.3.1)` since the morphism `Y' ‚Üí Y` is √©tale, hence flat and locally of finite presentation; one evidently has still
`X √ó_Y U = X √ó_Y U' = f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(U) √ó_U U'`. Since now the morphism `U' ‚Üí U` is faithfully flat and quasi-compact, one deduces
from `(2.7.1, (xv))` that the morphism `f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(U) ‚Üí U`, restriction of `f`, is finite, which proves the corollary.

**Remark (18.12.5).** ‚ÄĒ One will note that in the proof of `(18.12.4)` one has not used the hypothesis that `f` is
universally closed in its general form, but only that `f_{(Y')}` is a closed morphism for every √©tale morphism
`Y' ‚Üí Y`.

**Corollary (18.12.6).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.6 -->

*Let `f : X ‚Üí Y` be a morphism of preschemes. The following conditions are equivalent:*

*a) `f` is a closed immersion.*

*b) `f` is a proper monomorphism.*

*c) `f` is proper and, for every `y ‚ąą Y`, the `k(y)`-prescheme `X_y = f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y)` is radicial and geometrically reduced over
`k(y)` (i.e. empty or `k(y)`-isomorphic to `Spec(k(y))`).*

This is deduced from `(18.12.4)` as `(8.11.5)` is deduced from `(8.11.1)`.

**Proposition (18.12.7).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.7 -->

*Let `f : X ‚Üí Y` be a morphism locally of finite type, `y` a point of `Y`. In order that there exist an open
neighbourhood `U` of `y` such that the restriction `f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(U) ‚Üí U` of `f` be a closed immersion, it is necessary and
sufficient that `X_y` be a `k(y)`-prescheme radicial and geometrically reduced over `k(y)` (i.e. empty or
`k(y)`-isomorphic to `Spec(k(y))`) and that there exist an open neighbourhood `V` of `y` such that the restriction
`f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(V) ‚Üí V` of `f` be a universally closed morphism.*

The conditions being evidently necessary, let us prove that they are sufficient. One can restrict to the case where
`X_y ‚Č† ‚ąÖ`. By virtue of the second condition, one can already suppose `f` universally closed. Let us show moreover that
one can suppose `f` affine, hence separated; this results from the following lemma:

**Lemma (18.12.7.1).** *Let `f : X ‚Üí Y` be a closed morphism, `y ‚ąą Y` a point such that every neighbourhood of `X_y`
contains an affine neighbourhood of `X_y` (condition always verified when `X_y` is empty or reduced to a single point).
Then there exists an affine open neighbourhood `U` of `y` such that the restriction `f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(U) ‚Üí U` of `f` be an affine
morphism.*

Indeed, let `U_0` be an affine open neighbourhood of `y` in `Y` and let `V` be an affine open neighbourhood of `X_y`
contained in `f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(U_0)`. Since `f` is closed, there exists an affine open neighbourhood `U ‚äā U_0` of `y` such that
`f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(U) ‚äā V`. Since the restriction `g : V ‚Üí U_0` of `f` is an affine morphism, the same is true of its restriction
`f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(U) ‚Üí U` `(II, 1.2.5)`.

Suppose therefore `f` affine and universally closed, and let us show that there exists an open neighbourhood `U` of `y`
such that the restriction `f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(U) ‚Üí U` is a finite morphism; since one can suppose `Y` and `X` affine, one can suppose
`f` of finite type, hence proper, and it suffices to prove that there exists a neighbourhood `U` of `y` such that
`f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(U) ‚Üí U` is a quasi-finite morphism `(18.12.4)`. But there exists a neighbourhood `V` of the set `X_y` (reduced to
a single point) such that `f | V` is quasi-finite `(13.1.4)`, and since `f` is closed there is a neighbourhood `U` of
`y` such that `f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(U) ‚äā V`, which finishes the proof, taking account of `(18.12.6)`.

**Proposition (18.12.8).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.8 -->

*Let `f : X ‚Üí Y` be a morphism of preschemes. In order that `f` be integral, it is necessary and sufficient that `f` be
affine and universally closed.*

The conditions are necessary `(II, 6.1.10)`; let us prove that they are sufficient. One can suppose `Y = Spec(A)`
affine, hence also `X = Spec(B)`, and it must be proved that every element `b ‚ąą B` is integral over `A` `(II, 6.1.1)`.
Let `B'` be the sub-`A`-algebra of `B` generated by `b`, which is an `A`-algebra of finite type; set `X' = Spec(B')`,
so that `f : X ‚Üí Y` factors as `X ‚Üí^g X' ‚Üí^h Y`, where `h` is of finite type, and `g` is dominant since the
homomorphism `B' ‚Üí B` is injective `(I, 1.2.7)`. Since `h` is separated and `h ‚ąė g` universally closed, `g` is
universally closed `(II, 5.4.3 and `

<!-- original page 183 -->

`5.4.9)`, hence surjective since it is dominant; one concludes `(II, 5.4.3 and 5.4.9)` that `h` is also universally
closed, hence proper since it is of finite type and separated. But then, for every `y ‚ąą Y`, the morphism
`h‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y) ‚Üí Spec(k(y))` deduced from `h` is proper and affine, hence finite `(III, 4.4.2)`, in other words `h` is
quasi-finite; one deduces therefore from `(18.12.4)` that `h` is finite, which proves that `B'` is a finite `A`-algebra,
and consequently that `b` is integral over `A`. Q.E.D.

**Remark (18.12.9).** ‚ÄĒ It may be that a morphism `f : X ‚Üí Y` be integral when one supposes it only separated,
universally closed and such that for every `y ‚ąą Y`, the morphism `f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y) ‚Üí Spec(k(y))` deduced from `f` is integral. It
would be necessary for this to prove that these conditions imply that `f` is affine, or again that every fibre `X_y` is
contained in an affine open neighbourhood.

**Corollary (18.12.10).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.10 -->

*A morphism `f : X ‚Üí Y` which is injective and universally closed is integral.*

It suffices, by `(18.12.8)`, to prove that `f` is affine, which results from lemma `(18.12.7.1)` and from the
hypothesis.

**Corollary (18.12.11).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.11 -->

*Let `f : X ‚Üí Y` be a morphism of preschemes (resp. a morphism locally of finite type). In order that `f` be a
universal homeomorphism `(2.4.2)`, it is necessary and sufficient that `f` be integral (resp. finite), radicial and
surjective.*

One knows that the conditions are sufficient `(2.4.5)`; they are necessary by virtue of `(18.12.10)` and `(18.12.4)`.

The following proposition improves `(8.11.2)`:

**Proposition (18.12.12).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.12 -->

*Every morphism `f : X ‚Üí Y` which is quasi-finite and separated is quasi-affine.*

Set `ūĚíú = f_*(ūĚí™_X)`, which is a quasi-coherent `ūĚí™_Y`-algebra since `f` is quasi-compact and separated `(1.7.4)`; let
`Z = Spec(ūĚíú)` `(II, 1.3.1)` so that `f` factors canonically as `X ‚Üí^g Z ‚Üí^h Y`, `h` being affine and `g` corresponding
to the identity automorphism of `ūĚíú` `(II, 1.2.7)`; it will suffice to prove that `g` is an open immersion, or, what
amounts to the same `(17.9.1)`, that `g` is √©tale and radicial. It will evidently suffice to show that, for every
`y ‚ąą Y`, the morphism `g` is √©tale and radicial at each point of `f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y)`. Now, for every `y ‚ąą Y`, one can apply to `f`
the result of `(18.12.3)`, of which we preserve the notations; since the morphism `Y' ‚Üí Y` is flat, and that `f` is
quasi-compact and separated, one has, up to canonical isomorphism, `f'_*(ūĚí™_{X'}) = ūĚíú ‚äó_{ūĚí™_Y} ūĚí™_{Y'} = ūĚíú'` `(2.3.1)`,
so `Z' = Z √ó_Y Y'` identifies with `Spec(f'_*(ūĚí™_{X'}))`, and in the canonical factorization
`X' ‚Üí^{g'} Z' ‚Üí^{h'} Y'` of `f'` `(II, 1.2.7)`, one has `h' = h_{(Y')}` and `g' = g_{(Y')}`. This being so, the
decomposition of `X'` into the sum of two sub-preschemes `X'_1`, `X'_2` implies the decomposition of `ūĚíú'` into the
direct product of the two quasi-coherent `ūĚí™_{Y'}`-algebras `ūĚíú'_1`, `ūĚíú'_2`, direct images respectively of `ūĚí™_{X'_1}` and
`ūĚí™_{X'_2}`, so that `Z'` identifies with the sum `Z'_1 ‚äĒ Z'_2`, where `Z'_i = Spec(ūĚíú'_i)` and `g'(X'_i) ‚äā Z'_i` for
`i = 1, 2`. Since `X'_1` is finite over `Y'`, `g'_1 = g' | X'_1` is an isomorphism of `X'_1` onto `Z'_1`, since
`f' | X'_1` is affine; since `X'_2 ‚ą© f'‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y') = ‚ąÖ`, one sees that `g'` is √©tale and radicial at each point of
`f'‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y')`. The morphism `Y' ‚Üí Y` being flat and locally of finite presentation, one therefore deduces first from
`(17.7.4)` that `g` is √©tale at all points of `X` projections of points of `f'‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y')`, that is to say at all points of
`f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y)` `(I, 3.5.2)`. On the other hand, the morphism `g'_{y'} : f'‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y') ‚Üí h'‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y')` deduced from `g'` is radicial;
since `k(y') = k(y)`, the morphism `g_y : f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y) ‚Üí h‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y)` is also radicial, in other words `g` is radicial at each
point of `f‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(y)`, which finishes proving the proposition.

The following statement improves similarly `(8.12.6)`:

**Corollary (18.12.13)** *("Main Theorem" of Zariski).* ‚ÄĒ *Let `Y` be a quasi-compact and quasi-separated prescheme,
`f : X ‚Üí Y` a quasi-finite and separated morphism. Then there exists a factorization of `f`*

```text
  X ‚Üí^g Z ‚Üí^u Y
```

*where `g` is an open immersion (necessarily quasi-compact) and `u` a finite morphism.*

Indeed, it results from `(18.12.12)` that `f` is quasi-affine, hence quasi-projective. One can then apply `(8.12.8)`,
where the hypothesis of the existence of an ample `ūĚí™_Y`-Module can in fact be replaced by the sole hypothesis that `Y`
is quasi-compact and quasi-separated: indeed, it results from `(8.12.3)` that the existence of the announced
factorization in `(8.12.8)` is a property local on `Y`, and that it therefore suffices to prove it when `Y` is affine.

**Remark (18.12.14).** ‚ÄĒ One can give of `(18.12.13)` a proof analogous to that of `(18.12.12)` not using `(8.12.8)`
(but using `(18.12.3)`, hence `(18.5.11)`, which itself uses the "Main theorem" in its local form `(8.12.9)`). Let us
indeed keep the notations of the proof of `(18.12.12)`, and let `‚Ą¨` be the quasi-coherent `ūĚí™_Y`-Algebra, *integral
closure* of `ūĚí™_Y` in `ūĚíú` `(II, 6.3.2)`. If one sets `T = Spec(‚Ą¨)`, it suffices, by virtue of `(8.12.3)`, to prove that
the `Y`-morphism `gŐÉ : X ‚Üí T` corresponding to the canonical injection `‚Ą¨ ‚Üí ūĚíú` is an immersion, and for this it
suffices to show `(17.9.1)` that `gŐÉ` is √©tale and radicial. With the notations of `(18.12.12)`, one can suppose that
`Y = Spec(C)` and `Y' = Spec(C')` are affine, `C'` being an √©tale `C`-algebra `(17.3.2)`; hence `ūĚíú = √É`, where `A` is

<!-- original page 184 -->

a `C`-algebra, `ūĚíú' = √É'` with `A' = A ‚äó_C C'`, and `‚Ą¨ = BŐÉ`, where `B` is the integral closure of `C` in `A`. The
algebra `A'` is isomorphic to the product `A'_1 √ó A'_2`, where `A'_1` is a finite `C'`-algebra. It will suffice to
prove that `B' = B ‚äó_C C'`, which identifies by flatness with a sub-`C'`-algebra of `A'`, contains `A'_1`, for indeed
`B'` will then decompose into the product `A'_1 √ó A''_2`, where `A''_2` is a sub-`C'`-algebra of `A'_2`, and if one
sets `T'_2 = Spec(A''_2)`, `T' = T √ó_Y Y'` will be the sum of `Z'_1 = Spec(A'_1)` and `T'_2`, and `gŐÉ' | X'_1` will be
an isomorphism of `X'_1` onto `Z'_1`, which will allow one to conclude as in `(18.12.12)`.

To prove that `B'` contains `A'_1`, it evidently suffices to prove the following proposition, which extends partially
`(6.14.4)` when one no longer makes Noetherian hypotheses:

**Proposition (18.12.15).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.15 -->

*Let `C` be a ring, `C'` an √©tale `C`-algebra, `A` a `C`-algebra, `B` the integral closure of `C` in `A`; one sets
`A' = A ‚äó_C C'`, `B' = B ‚äó_C C'`, `B'` being identified with a sub-algebra of `A'`; then `B'` is the integral closure
of `C'` in `A'`.*

By considering the filtered increasing family of sub-`C`-algebras of finite type of `A` and reasoning as in
`(6.14.4, II)`, one can first suppose that `A` is a `C`-algebra of finite type, hence of the form `E/ūĚĒć`, where
`E = C[T_1, ‚Ä¶, T_r]` and `ūĚĒć` is an ideal of `E`; one has then `A' = E'/ūĚĒć E'`, where `E' = C'[T_1, ‚Ä¶, T_r]`. Let
`(ūĚĒć_őĽ)` be the filtered increasing family of ideals of finite type of `E` contained in `ūĚĒć`, so that `A` is the
inductive limit of the `E/ūĚĒć_őĽ`; if `B_őĽ` is the integral closure of `C` in `E/ūĚĒć_őĽ`, `B` is the inductive limit of the
`B_őĽ`, as the reasoning of `(5.13.4)` shows. Similarly the integral closure of `C'` in `E'/ūĚĒć E'` is the inductive limit
of the integral closure of `C'` in `E'/ūĚĒć_őĽ E'`; if one proves that the latter is equal to `B_őĽ ‚äó_C C'`, it will result
that `B' = lim^‚Üí (B_őĽ ‚äó_C C')` will be the integral closure of `C'` in `A'`. One is thus reduced to proving the
proposition when `A` is a `C`-algebra of finite presentation.

Let us next show that one can reduce to the case where `C` is Noetherian. Indeed, `C` is the filtered union of its
sub-`‚Ą§`-algebras of finite type `C_őĪ`, so it results from `(17.7.8)` that there exists an index `őĪ` and an √©tale
`C_őĪ`-algebra `C'_őĪ` such that `C' = C'_őĪ ‚äó_{C_őĪ} C`; moreover `C'` is the inductive limit of the
`C'_ő≤ = C'_őĪ ‚äó_{C_őĪ} C_ő≤` for `ő≤ ‚Č• őĪ`. One can moreover suppose, since `A` is a `C`-algebra of finite presentation,
that `A = A_őĪ ‚äó_{C_őĪ} C`, where `A_őĪ` is a `C_őĪ`-algebra of finite type, and `A` is the inductive limit of the
`A_ő≤ = A_őĪ ‚äó_{C_őĪ} C_ő≤` for `ő≤ ‚Č• őĪ` `(8.9.1)`. The reasoning of `(5.13.4)` then shows that `B` is the inductive limit
of the integral closures `B_ő≤` of the `C_ő≤` in the `A_ő≤`. Similarly `A'` is the inductive limit of the
`A'_ő≤ = A_ő≤ ‚äó_{C_ő≤} C'_ő≤ = A_őĪ ‚äó_{C_őĪ} C'_ő≤` for `ő≤ ‚Č• őĪ`, hence the same reasoning as above shows that it will suffice
to prove that `B'_ő≤ = B_ő≤ ‚äó_{C_ő≤} C'_ő≤` is the integral closure of `C'_ő≤` in `A'_ő≤`.

Once reduced to the case where `C` is Noetherian, the proposition becomes a particular case of `(6.14.4)`. One must
nevertheless observe that, when `C'` is supposed √©tale over `C` Noetherian, the proof of `(6.14.4)` no longer requires
the delicate theorem `(6.14.1)`. Indeed, the successive reductions of the proof of `(6.14.4)` reduce, without using
`(6.14.1)`, to the case where `C` is integral, `A` the field of fractions of `C`. Since then `B` is a normal ring and
the morphism `Spec(B') ‚Üí Spec(B)` is √©tale, it results from `(17.5.7)` that `B'` is a normal ring; the reasoning ends
by appealing only to the elementary lemma `(6.14.1.1)`, but not to the difficult part of the proof of `(6.14.1)`.

**Proposition (18.12.16).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.16 -->

*Let `g : Y ‚Üí S` be a quasi-compact morphism, `f : X ‚Üí Y` a separated and quasi-finite morphism. For every invertible
`ūĚí™_Y`-Module `‚Ąí`, ample relative to `S` `(II, 4.6.1)`, the `ūĚí™_X`-Module `f*(‚Ąí)` is ample relative to `S`.*

Indeed, by virtue of `(18.12.12)`, the morphism `f` is quasi-affine, hence `(II, 5.1.6)` the `ūĚí™_X`-Module `ūĚí™_X` is
ample for `f`. One deduces `(II, 4.6.13, (ii))` that `ūĚí™_X ‚äó_{ūĚí™_Y} f*(‚Ąí^{‚äó n}) = f*(‚Ąí^{‚äó n})` is ample relative to `S`
for `n` large enough. But since `f*(‚Ąí^{‚äó n}) = (f*(‚Ąí))^{‚äó n}`, this implies that `f*(‚Ąí)` is ample relative to `S`
`(II, 4.6.9, (i))`.

**Corollary (18.12.17).**

<!-- label: IV.18.12.17 -->

*Let `Z` be an affine scheme, `h : X ‚Üí Z` a morphism of finite type, `‚Ąí` an invertible `ūĚí™_X`-Module. With the notations
of `(II, 4.5.2)`, the conditions of `(II, 4.5.2)` (which are equivalent to the fact that `‚Ąí` is ample) are also
equivalent to each of the following:*

*b'') `h` is separated, one has `G(s) = X` and the canonical morphism `u : G(s) ‚Üí Proj(S)` has its fibres finite and
discrete.*

*b''') One has `G(s) = X` and the canonical morphism `u` is radicial.*

If `Z = Spec(A)`, the ring `S` is canonically equipped with a structure of graded `A`-algebra, so one has a structural
morphism `g : Proj(S) ‚Üí Z` which is separated `(II, 2.4.2)`, and one has `h = g ‚ąė u`.

Since every radicial morphism is separated `(1.8.7.1)`, b''') implies that `h` is separated, hence implies b''). Since
condition b) of `(II, 4.5.2)` evidently implies b''), it remains to see that b'') implies that `‚Ąí` is ample. Since
`h = g ‚ąė u` is of finite type by hypothesis and `g` is separated, `u` is also of finite type `(I, 6.3.4)`, hence the
hypothesis b'') implies that `u` is quasi-finite and separated `(I, 5.5.1)`. To prove that `‚Ąí` is ample, we shall apply
`(18.12.16)`. Set `Y = Proj(S)`. Since `X` is quasi-compact, there exist an integer `n > 0` and a finite number of
elements `f_j ‚ąą S_n` such that the inverse images `u‚ĀĽ¬Ļ(D_+(f_j))` cover `X`; one can therefore consider `u` as a
quasi-finite and separated morphism of `X` into the open `Y' = ‚čÉ D_+(f_j)` of `Y`. Consider then the invertible
`ūĚí™_{Y'}`-Module `‚Ąí' = ūĚí™_Y(n) | Y'` `(II, 2.5.8)`; it is very ample relative to `Z` `(II, 4.4.3)`, and `u*(‚Ąí')` is none
other by definition than `‚Ąí^{‚äó n}`

`(II, 3.7.9, (i))`. By virtue of `(18.12.16)`, `‚Ąí^{‚äó n}` is therefore ample relative to `Z` (which is equivalent to
saying that it is ample `(II, 4.6.6)`), and consequently the same is true of `‚Ąí` `(II, 4.5.6, (i))`.

We leave to the reader the task of stating similarly conditions equivalent to those of `(II, 4.6.3)` for
`ūĚí™_X`-Modules relatively ample.
